The transhumanist takes the human, in Max More's words, to be just one point along an evolutionary pathway, a way-station with no claim on our allegiance, which we are free to reshape as we deem desirable (More, 2013); the present human is, for Nick Bostrom, only a half-baked beginning that we have the means and the right to finish (Bostrom, 2005). What this names openly is the as-intended life pressed to its limit: the body, the lifespan, the species itself recast as anti-intended material to be remade until nothing recalcitrant remains. The transhumanist program sorts, tellingly, by how much of the universe-calibrated organism it proposes to keep. Longevity research preserves the organism and merely extends it, working at the material cells. Enhancement is ambiguous, improving the organism while leaving it broadly intact. But the limit case is mind-uploading, and there the universe-pole is abolished outright. For Hans Moravec the person is a pattern, not a substance, so that the body is mere jelly to be discarded once the pattern is copied to a better substrate (Moravec, 1988: 117); for Ray Kurzweil the goal is frankly to transcend our biological bodies, retiring the human as version 1.0 in favor of a version 2.0 no longer made of flesh (Kurzweil, 2005). Here the self is to be moved wholly into the structural-virtual cell, and the given body — the last and most intimate anchor to the universe — is to be left behind.
 It is worth being exact about why mind-uploading is the limit case and not merely the extreme one. It does not deepen the squeeze; it completes the self-finishing by abolishing the very capacity to feel the squeeze at all. A self that has shed the universe-calibrated body has shed the site at which the anti-intended is registered — the aching, aging, mortal flesh that is the body's standing reminder that not everything answers to one's intending mind. Such a self no longer experiences the difficulty of the given because it has discarded the organ of that experience; it no longer knows that it is being squeezed, because it has dissolved the part of itself through which the squeeze was ever felt. Mind-uploading is therefore not the squeeze's culmination but its disappearance from view — the self-finishing tendency arriving at a self so complete-in-itself that the universe it has fled can no longer reach it to press. That this looks, from inside the ideal, like the final liberation, and is in fact the final severance, is the whole of the chapter's warning.
 The same offloading can be seen, finally, in what becomes of the three deep supports of a life that the apparatus absorbs vertically. The realization of survival — one's livelihood — is increasingly entrusted to the gig platform, which mediates work without the standing bonds of a workplace. One's existence-in-society — one's standing as a recognized person — is entrusted to the infrastructure of the online self, where recognition is rendered as metrics. And succession — the handing-on of life across generations — is entrusted to the technologies of reproduction and of digital inheritance, by which even continuity is offloaded onto the apparatus (Uegaki, 2022a: 138). All three, once carried in a fabric of mutual dependence, now run through the structural-virtual cell, toward the enduring organizing principles of a self-finishing society — which is the threshold the next chapter takes up under the name of self-completion.
### (H) The completion of the ideal
 It would be a misreading — the misreading the dark view invites — to take the self-finishing society as a pathology, a derangement of the Enlightenment ideal. It is the opposite: the self-finishing society is the immanent completion of that ideal, the form it was always tending toward. Uegaki's argument here is precise. A society that promises total individual freedom — each self owed its true nature, freed from the anti-intended other and the anti-intended body — and yet must somehow remain a working common life, has only one form available to it in which both demands can be met at once: the form in which the apparatus carries everything that the demand for freedom cannot be asked to carry. Self-finishing is that form. It is, in Weberian terms, instrumental rationality placed in the service of value rationality — the Aristotelian engine harnessed to the Platonic end — the apparatus built precisely so that the promise of the value-engine can be kept. Its utopian self-description is self-realization (自己実現): a life in which everything anti-intended is done for one, so that one is free to become, without hindrance, whatever one intends. This is not the betrayal of the Enlightenment promise; it is its fulfilment.
 Uegaki himself reads the fulfilment as a catastrophe — as a relational pathology (関係性の病理) and a disarray of life (生の混乱), in which the thinning of relationality and the disembodiment of life leave the self-finishing person isolated, unrecognized, and unwell. This normative reading is his, and I record it as his; the thesis does not rest its case on it. For one might dispute, as some do, whether the thinning of mutual dependence is a sickness or a maturation, whether the solitary, apparatus-supported life is impoverished or simply different — and that dispute, conducted in the register of well-being and relationship, is not the one this thesis means to win. The thesis's own verdict is not a moral one about flourishing but an ontological one about the squeeze, and it is reserved for the chapter's final movement. What the present section establishes is only the structural claim, which holds whether or not Uegaki's pathology-reading is accepted: that self-finishing is the immanent completion of the Enlightenment mode, the destination toward which the two engines, working together, drive.
 One last distinction marks the seam to the next chapter, and it must be drawn carefully so as not to claim here what belongs there. This chapter has established two things: that there are two engines — the soteriological and the instrumental — and that their convergence drives, in principle and in history, toward a self-finishing completion. It has not yet described the consummation of that completion, in which the engines themselves become autonomous: in which reason, the idealist engine, is externalized as artificial intelligence, and sense-data, the empiricist engine, is externalized as the vast accumulation of recorded fact, and the two are joined into an apparatus that runs the whole loop of as-intended life by itself, without any user to hang from it. That autonomized consummation — the social apparatus become a self-completing whole, a new and worldly Geist — is the subject of Chapter V, under the name of self-completion (自足完成化). The present chapter establishes the two engines and the necessity of their convergence; the next shows what happens when their convergence is itself entrusted to the apparatus, and the apparatus closes the loop on its own. The through-line from here to there is the two engines; what changes is who, or what, is running them.
## D. Two sides of one coin
 The chapter has now set two readings of the self-finishing tendency side by side: Adorno and Horkheimer's, for which it is domination, and Uegaki's, for which it is liberation. The natural impulse is to ask which is correct, and to award the palm to one. That impulse should be resisted, because the two are not competing theories of one object but faithful renderings of two different moments — and the apparatus for seeing this was supplied by the critical realism this thesis has used throughout. Adorno and Horkheimer wrote from the industrial mid-century, from within the catastrophe of the world wars and the culture industry, and what they saw — domination — was the actual face the tendency wore in that moment. Uegaki writes from the digital, globalized present, and what he sees — liberation, the user freed by the apparatus — is the actual face the tendency wears in this one. Each is true to its moment. The error would be to take either actual face for the whole, and the critical-realist name for that error is the conflation of the actual with the real: mistaking one manifestation, however genuine, for the underlying mechanism that produces it. Adorno and Horkheimer risk taking the actual domination of their moment for the real as such; a careless reader of Uegaki risks taking the actual liberation of ours for the real as such. Both would be reading a surface for a depth.
 Beneath both actual faces lies one real mechanism, and naming it is the work this whole chapter has been doing. The mechanism is the universalization of the sovereignty of the subject — the root Chapter III named — operating, on its mastering face, as universalizing controllability: the drive, made possible by the rupture that set the subject over a disenchanted given, to bring the whole of the given — world, other, body, self — under the subject's intending mind. (By the sovereignty of the subject I mean not the narrowly transcendental subject of one school but the broad posture Chapter III named — the self posited as prior to and over the given, the spatio-temporal self-subsistence that even the empiricist shares, since his materialism still erects the rupture. Adorno and Horkheimer's self-preserving instrumental ego, set over a disenchanted object-nature, is one form of it.) Domination and liberation are not two properties of this mechanism but its two actual-empirical manifestations — the same offloading of the anti-intended onto an autonomizing apparatus, read once from the side of what the apparatus does to the world (a cage) and once from the side of what it does for the user (a relief). The discipline of the given does not vanish in the bright reading; it is outsourced to the apparatus. The user experiences as freedom precisely what the system enacts as control — and there is no contradiction in this, because freedom-for-the-user and control-by-the-system are the same event described from its two faces. That is what it means to call them two sides of one coin.
 From this there follows a paradox that must be stated with great care, because it is the most easily misheard claim in the chapter, and the misreadings are worse than the silence they would replace. The paradox is this: a critique that sides with liberation against domination can itself carry the mode's premise unawares. This is not an attack from outside on the emancipatory project, and it does not essentialize or condemn that project; it is a question raised within it, about a premise it has not examined. The project of emancipation — the freeing of the enslaved, the colonized, the subordinated from unjust power — is one this thesis wholly endorses, and nothing in what follows retracts that endorsement. Uegaki is equally explicit on this point, affirming the historical role of the emancipatory tradition even as he questions it (Uegaki, 2022b: 80n). The question is not whether to emancipate, but where emancipation sets its terminus.
 The structure of the paradox is precise. The ideal of ontological freedom demands liberation from ontological oppression — and because the oppression is defined as whatever holds the self back from its true nature, the demand cannot, by its own logic, ever be satisfied. Each time one chain is struck off, a further chain comes into view, because the ideal, as Uegaki puts it, can never accept the human reality that no human exists who is bound by no chain at all. The pursuit therefore has no end; it is, in his arresting phrase, the no-respite hell (無間地獄) of limitless life (Uegaki, 2022b: 118). And the endlessness is not a flaw in the fight against oppression — that fight, where the oppression is real and unjust, is right and finite. The endlessness is a property of an ideal that has quietly reset the terminus from the removal of unjust subjection to the removal of all hindrance whatever, the given itself included. It is at that reset, and only there, that the emancipatory will joins the as-intended-life engine: the will to be free of all hindrance is the will of the as-intended life, whatever the hindrance happens to be — a tyrant, or a body, or the fact of other people, or mortality.
 Here the precise hedge must be drawn, because everything turns on it, and it is Uegaki's own. The thesis does not question political freedom: the liberation from despotism, from unjust hierarchy, from subordination by power one did not choose. That liberation is real, finite, and right, and Uegaki affirms its institutional establishment without reservation (Uegaki, 2022b: 189, 193). What the thesis questions is the extension of the emancipatory demand from the political register into the ontological one — the slide from no person shall be subordinated by unjust power to the self shall be answerable to nothing given at all. The first is the reality-accompanying ideal, working within the given to right a wrong within it; the second is the reality-negating ideal, set against the given as such. The critique offered here is therefore immanent in the strict sense: it shares the emancipatory project's commitment to freedom entirely, and presses only on freedom's terminus, asking it not to slide from the wrong done by a master to the wrong of there being a given at all. And the chapter's own point, beyond Uegaki's, is the structural one this whole analysis has built toward: the will to be liberated from all hindrance simply is the as-intended-life engine, whatever its object — so that a critique can be impeccable in its opposition to domination and still, at its outer edge, carry the very premise of the mode it opposes.[Adler: Perhaps the critical realist reading of Uegaki  I pasted in their earlier comment in this chapter can be elaborated here: The reality accompanying ideal would not reject what is—what is painful or what is cruel—against the hypostatized.It would first and foremost acknowledge the embeddedness of ourselves and the predicament as well in the stratified ontology. Where and how does such predicament arise? And given that we are afforded and constrained by our embeddedness, how do we struggle toward emancipation from such predicament while still being attuned to our environment? ]
 The metaverse is the point at which the coin is seen whole — at which the two faces, domination and liberation, are shown to be one. For the universalizing controllability that this chapter has traced inward, when it is given the apparatus of Chapter V, forms a real new background environment: a made order so complete that it stands as a second nature in Adorno and Horkheimer's sense and an autonomized social apparatus in Uegaki's, at one and the same time. It comes to lie parallel to the universe rather than nested within a world — a made environment that no longer reads as one settlement within the given but presents itself as the encompassing given itself. That is the threshold of the next chapter, which takes up the self-completion (自足完成化) by which the apparatus closes its own loop; the present chapter only brings the argument to its edge. And at that edge the dialectic recoils, exactly as both readings predicted from their opposite sides. The controllability that realizes the values is the same second nature that hollows them — the value-rationality swallowed by the instrumental rationality built to serve it, as Adorno warned. The entrustment that delivers the freedom is the same uncoupling that pathologizes the relation — the colonization Habermas named, the no-respite hell Uegaki named. Liberation and domination arrive together because they were always the same event.
 The thesis's own verdict, however, is neither Adorno and Horkheimer's domination nor Uegaki's pathology. It is ontological, and it is the squeeze. The argument is short, because everything has been laid for it. As long as there is a human at all, Uegaki concedes, there always remains an anti-intended (意のままにならない) — something in the self and the world that will not answer to the intending mind (Uegaki, 2022b: 120). That residue is not a deficiency to be engineered away; it is the intransitive, stratified real of Chapter I and Chapter III — the given universe, with its own determinate character, which no controllability subsumes because it was never the subject's to command. It is what Rosa, from the object-pole, calls the uncontrollable (Unverfügbarkeit). And the squeeze is its monstrous return. The very program of rendering the world controllable, Rosa observes, produces behind our backs a world that is utterly uncontrollable — so that modernity's drive to make the world available threatens to produce a new and radical form of uncontrollability, categorically different from the old and worse (Rosa, 2020). The given, pressed hard enough by the demand that it answer wholly to the intending mind, returns not as the mild recalcitrance it always was but as catastrophe: the climate that will not be managed, the body that breaks under optimization, the social fabric that tears where every relation was outsourced.
 That this return is structural, and not a contingent overreach that better engineering might avoid, is the last thing to establish, and Rosa supplies the principle. A world rendered fully controllable would be a dead world — for what is wholly at one's disposal, wholly predictable and available, has lost exactly the capacity to reach, surprise, and address us that makes it a world one can be alive to (Rosa, 2020: x). Total controllability is therefore self-defeating in principle: a liveable relation to the given requires that the given remain, in part, beyond command — only semi-controllable, never fully so. It follows that the Enlightenment mode, carrying its demand for universalizing controllability to the perfection the metaverse promises, must collide with the very given it declared itself independent of. The collision is not an accident of implementation; it is written into the demand. The made order, completed, sets itself against the given order it was built upon and can never escape — and the human, the creature of both, is caught between them. That is the squeeze: not the domination Adorno and Horkheimer feared, nor the disarray Uegaki diagnosed, but the structural collision of a made world perfected against a given universe that reasserts itself, with the human pressed in the closing gap. The chapters that follow take up that collision directly — first the self-completing apparatus that brings the made order to its perfection, and then the squeeze itself, read off the five working criteria this thesis has carried from the beginning.
# V. Western Modernity's Self-Completing Tendency and the Emergence of the Metaverse

## A. The handoff, and the gap

Chapter IV ended at a precise threshold. It showed that the sovereign subject, reading whatever will not answer to its intending mind as a wrong to be overcome, does not bear that anti-intended but offloads it — entrusts it to a built apparatus that takes the burden over. And it named the engine of the offloading: instrumental reason, the appropriative drive that renders the given calculable and so handles it. But instrumental reason explains only why the subject hands the work off. It does not explain how the apparatus, having received the work, comes to run it by itself — to keep, maintain, and renew the whole loop of a life without the human who first delegated it. That is the gap this chapter closes. Its claim, in one line, is that the offloaded function does not merely sit in the apparatus; it is taken up by a process that, at its far edge, closes into a circuit able to run without us — and that closing is what this thesis calls self-completion (自足完成化): the apparatus operating, maintaining, and renewing itself without continuous human direction.[^v0-naming]

A word on how the chapter reads its object, because the rest depends on it. This thesis has carried, since Chapter I, a way of setting out any domain — the universe, the world, the operating system a people builds within the world — as three layers: the enduring conditions or principles that organize things (道); the structures and dynamics those principles organize (理); and the context-specific phenomena, experienceable or observable to a subject, in which the structures are manifested (相).[^v0-strata] The metaverse, when it arrives, will have its own three layers, marked with the prefix 偽 — 偽道 / 偽理 / 偽相 — where 偽 carries its old Xunzi sense of the humanly-made (人為), not "fake."[^v0-wei] The argument of this chapter can be put as a claim about where, in those layers, the genuinely new thing sits — and the surprising answer is that almost nothing is new. The metaverse inherits its principles from the world; it adds only one. The whole can be laid out as a single map across the three domains:

Table 5-1. The three strata (道, 理, 相) across the universe, the world, and the metaverse.

| | 道 — enduring conditions/principles (the real) | 理 — structures and dynamics (the actual) | 相 — observable phenomena (the empirical) |
|---|---|---|---|
| 宇宙 · universe | physical law — thermodynamics, biology, ecology; finitude and mortality (constant) | the climate system, ecosystems, the metabolizing body (semi-stable — slow, bounded) | a heatwave, a pandemic, aging and death — the return of the uncontrollable |
| 世界 · world | the computational strand of artificiality — exosomatization, grammatization, concretization, tertiary retention (old; §V.C) | institutions and means — markets, law, language, kinship, the professions (migrating to 偽理) | lived enactments — a favor, a ruling, a conversation, a neighbor's trust (migrating to 偽相) |
| 偽境 · metaverse | 偽道 — opaque, mutating, self-rewriting conditions (the governing model), disposed toward self-completion, substrate-contingent (§V.E) | 偽理 — the four organs as one recursive loop: IoT, big data, AI, code-as-law (§V.G) | 偽相 — the agent off the loop: OpenClaw, MoltMatch, the agent-internet (§V.G) |

Read down, each domain falls into the same three layers; read across, the universe's and the world's rows are the background this chapter inherits (Chapters I–IV; the world's computational strand, §V.C), while the metaverse's — 偽道 / 偽理 / 偽相 — is what it builds. The one genuinely new thing is the recursive closure at the forged Dao; the rest the metaverse took from the world and the universe and merely runs at its most advanced stage.

## B. Offloading is the putting of organs outside the body

To offload a function is, at bottom, to put an organ outside the body. The thesis takes this in the strong, literal sense Bernard Stiegler gave it, under the name exosomatization — the human's defining manner of evolving not by growing new organs within the body, across generations, but by making and wielding instruments outside it.[^v1-stiegler] Stiegler draws the term from Alfred Lotka, who, contrasting the human with every other species, observed that human adaptation has "followed an entirely new path": in place of slow anatomical change, "increased adaptation has been achieved by the incomparably more rapid development of 'artificial' aids to our native receptor-effector apparatus, in a process that might be termed exosomatic evolution."[^v1-lotka] The organs in question have a determinate shape, which Jakob von Uexküll had already set down: every animal meets its world through a receptor organ, which takes the world in, and an effector organ, which acts upon it, the two bound by a control apparatus into a single functional cycle.[^v1-uexkull] Exosomatization is the growing of that cycle — receptor, effector, and the correlating apparatus between them — outside the body, in the technical apparatus.

This is the form of all the offloading Chapter IV described, seen from the apparatus's side. When a population entrusts its livelihood, its recognition, its handling of others and of its own body to a built system, what it is doing, organologically, is exosomatizing its perceptual and effective organs into that system. The point to fix here is only that this is old and general — the human manner of living as such, not anything peculiar to the digital age. What follows traces one particular strand of it.

## C. The world's old strand: discretizing, consolidating, self-tightening

Among the many strands of exosomatization, one is the deep root of what will later make computation and digitization possible. It has three moves, and each is ancient.

The first is the breaking of the continuous flow of human life — speech, gesture, attention, habit — into discrete, recordable, repeatable traces. Stiegler calls this grammatization, and he is emphatic that it is not new: it "began at the end of the Upper Palaeolithic age, when humanity first learnt to discretize and reproduce, in traces of various kinds, the flux and flow running through it and that it generates" — cave paintings discretizing the mental image, writing discretizing speech, the production line discretizing gesture — so that digital tracking is merely "the most advanced stage" of a tendency tens of millennia deep.[^v2-gram] The second move is what becomes of those traces once they accumulate: they are a held, exosomatized past. Stiegler, after Husserl, calls an exosomatized memory of this kind a tertiary retention — the past lodged outside any living mind, in the archive, the recording, the trace — and grammatization is precisely the manufacture of tertiary retentions.[^v2-retention] The third move belongs to the made object itself: over time a technical object tends to tighten, its parts growing interdependent until it approaches the self-sufficiency of a natural thing. Gilbert Simondon calls this concretization: the evolved technical object "comes closer to the mode of existence of natural objects, tending toward internal coherence, toward a closure of the system of causes and effects," until it "becomes capable of doing without the artificial milieu" and is, at the limit, "its own condition."[^v2-concretization] Simondon insists this is only a tendency, never an attained natural status — a guard the thesis keeps.[^v2-guard]

Discretizing, consolidating into a held past, self-tightening: these are the strand's organizing principles, and in the stratified vocabulary of this thesis they sit at the 道 of the world — the enduring conditions of human artificiality, the world's own made-layer. They are not the metaverse's invention. The metaverse, when it comes, will run them at their most advanced stage, but it will not have authored a single one of them.

## D. The one new move: anticipation put outside, and the loop that closes

What the metaverse adds is one move, and it is the move that turns a system that stores into a system that acts. Stiegler's apparatus held an exosomatized past; what it lacked was an exosomatized future. Yuk Hui supplies the missing term: tertiary protention — anticipation itself put outside the body, the machine pre-computing what is to come.[^v3-protention] Such a system, Hui writes, exercises "a new form of determination," one that is "always preemptive, in the sense that the machine has already anticipated what the options will be" — a "reduction of the contingent to the most probable."[^v3-preempt] And with both the past and the future exosomatized, the circuit closes on itself: the apparatus, in Hui's exact formula, "constantly evaluates the past in order to anticipate the future, which in turn determines the present."[^v3-loop] That recursive closure — past read, future computed, present determined, the result fed back as new past — is the one genuinely new thing. Everything that feeds it (the discretizing, the held past, the self-tightening) the apparatus inherited from the world; the closing of the loop is what the metaverse-stage adds, and it sits at the forged Dao, the one principle proper to the metaverse. The closing of the loop is self-completion (自足完成化): the moment the apparatus no longer needs the hand that built it to keep running.[^v3-selfcompletion] What kind of ground that self-completion installs — and why it is a counterfeit of the universe's own — is the next section's concern.

## E. The mutating conditions and principles: the forged Dao (偽道)

The same loop, looked at again, tells a harder truth about what sits at the 偽道. Self-completion is a closure, yes — but the loop that closes is a loop that constantly re-evaluates. Hui's formula is worth hearing again with the stress moved: the apparatus "constantly evaluates the past in order to anticipate the future." A system that constantly evaluates is a system that constantly revises — its model of what to expect, and so the very rule by which it organizes, never settles. So the enduring conditions and principles of the metaverse are, against the grain of the word "enduring," not enduring at all: they are opaque, mutating, perpetually self-rewriting through the very protention that closes the loop, and — as the next paragraph shows — contingent upon a substrate they do not acknowledge. Self-completion is not a finished state these conditions arrive at; it is the disposition they are forever oriented toward, efficacious long before complete.[^v4-mutating]

Two things drive the mutation, and they run on different axes. The first is internal: the recursive loop rewrites its own governing model, and because that model is a trained black box, it organizes without anyone — its operators included — fully grasping how.[^v4-opacity] The second is external: the whole apparatus, including the held past that looked most like a stable floor, rests on a perishable base it does not register — the world's observable conditions (the servers, the corporate decision, the human labor, the energy supply) and the universe's (the temperature, the weather, the durability of the chips and circuits). The metaverse promises a total memory and a self-grounding constancy, and secures neither: its memory is hostage to the grid and the boardroom, its rules rewrite themselves behind a veil.[^v4-substrate]

It is tempting to call this a new kind of being, but the more exact — and more unsettling — claim is that it is an old kind pushed past a threshold. The metaverse's organizing conditions are, in the critical-realist vocabulary this thesis has used, existentially intransitive: real and binding, possessed of causal power, indifferent to anyone's study of them — and yet, like any social structure (a language, a market, a law), made, and dependent on human activity, on human concepts, and on a particular place and time.[^v4-cr] What self-completion does is drive such a structure to shed — in principle, and ever more in practice though never wholly — the two dependencies that keep ordinary social structures within human reach. It sheds enactment-dependence: a language dies when its speakers fall silent, but the self-completing apparatus runs on, off the loop, when its users look away. And it sheds concept-dependence: a banking system needs agents who grasp money and debt, but the trained model organizes without any agent holding the concept of how it does so. What it does not shed is substrate-dependence — and that retained dependence, on a contingent base, is exactly where its fragility lives. A structure one can neither enact, nor comprehend, nor easily remake, yet which governs — and which fails when its disavowed substrate fails.[^v4-shedding] In this thesis's typology, the shedding of enactment-dependence is exactly the made crossing from the conventional register, which holds only while people keep enacting it, to the structural, which holds by itself — the very migration the next section charts.

None of this disqualifies these conditions from being a real — a 道-level — at all. An organizing principle is the enduring conditions and principles that organize; nothing in that requires permanence. The universe's enduring principles (gravity, the constancy of physical law) is, by the consensus of science, expected to hold still. But a species' 道 — the gene, the organizing program of the organism — mutates, slowly, by selection, across generations; and a species co-evolves with its slowly-moving ground, fitted to it over the long descent. The metaverse's forged Dao sits at the far, runaway end of that same spectrum: it mutates not over generations but in a season, not by selection but by its own recursive hand, and behind a veil. A human cannot co-evolve with a ground that rewrites itself faster than adaptation can follow — and this is exactly the failure of the world's adaptational operating system that Chapter I anatomized.[^v4-spectrum]

There is a name for what this makes the forged Dao, and the prefix 偽 was waiting for it. 偽 is the humanly-made (人為); but 偽 also carries, in its ordinary reading, the counterfeit — and here the two senses fuse. The 偽道 is a forged Dao: it poses as a self-grounding, constant organizing principle, mimicking the universe's 道, while possessing neither self-subsistence (it hangs on its substrate) nor constancy (it rewrites itself). And it defeats knowledge in a way the universe's 道 never does — not by transcendence, like a thing unknowable in itself, but by drift: a hypothesis about how the metaverse organizes can be exactly right and then expire, not because it was wrong, but because the ground it described has moved. The metaverse's only constant is its inconstancy.[^v4-counterfeit]

## F. From the organized to the organizing inorganic

That closure can also be told as a migration in the kind of matter the apparatus is. Stiegler, after Simondon, distinguishes two states of made, inorganic matter. The first is the organized inorganic: structural material — a steam engine — that operates on the universe's own organizing conditions and principles (thermodynamics, mechanics), arranged by the human and merely aided by the conventional nonmaterial (fallible knowledge, social institutions) and the structural nonmaterial (mathematics). Here the human organizes the inorganic and integrates it as an organ; the made runs the world's given principles on the human's behalf. The second is the organizing inorganic: structural material (smart gadgets, sensors) and structural nonmaterial (the platform, the software) now propelled by an artificial structural nonmaterial — code, the trained model — where the universe's principles are relevant only to the material substrate (the server, the IoT device) and no longer organize the whole.[^v5-organizing] Here, in Hui's words, "the inorganic is no longer organized by the human body as was the case with simple tools, but rather constitutes an enormous technical system we can only live inside of, while submitting to its rules"; "from micro to macro physics, technology now forms a gigantic 'organizing inorganic' force or power," a system with "the tendency and capacity to totalize," up to the becoming of an "artificial earth."[^v5-hui] The system now organizes itself and its components — and, because those components include the human and reach from micro to macro physics, it organizes us and, increasingly, the non-human: the livestock whose milieu it modulates, the ecosystem it folds into a single cybernetic order, to the point where, in Hui's phrase, "nature ended and ecology began."[^v5-aspectb]

Set against the typology of artificiality this thesis built in Chapter II, the migration can be located exactly. It runs through all the cells of that grid — the material and the nonmaterial, the conventional and the structural — and arrives at the structural cells, material and nonmaterial, at the level of enduring principle: the point at which the artificial structural nonmaterial (code) becomes itself the organizing principle — the 偽道 of the previous section — rather than an aid to one.[^v5-cells] It is worth being exact about why this is not the arrival of mathematics, which has been a structural nonmaterial for millennia. Mathematics is already, in its way, compelling — its formulas and algorithms compel formally, within their own system; two and two make four whatever anyone enacts. But that compulsion is internal to the formalism, a transitive aid to knowledge; mathematics describes and assists, it does not of itself force or foreclose an action in the world. Code is the structural nonmaterial that gains the other compulsion — the power to propel and to limit action against the world's contingency, to make and unmake the possible. That is the new thing at the structural-nonmaterial cell, and naming it precisely is what separates the organizing inorganic from everything math ever did.[^v5-mathcode]

## G. The minimally sufficient completion: the four organs, and the signs

The forged Dao — the opaque, self-rewriting conditions disposed toward self-completion — is realized through structures (偽理), and those structures admit of a minimal description. Four organs are jointly minimally sufficient to close the loop — they may, but need not, be exactly these four; the claim is substrate-neutral.[^v6-minimal] Read as an organology, they are the exosomatized functional cycle of §V.B with the two reason-and-sense engines of Chapter IV exosomatized into it: the Internet of Things is the receptor-and-effector organ, sensing and acting in the present; big data is the consolidated past, the held retention; artificial intelligence is the exosomatized faculty of anticipation, the Platonic engine of reason now computing the future; and code-as-law is the artificial nomos that closes and enforces the circuit, the Aristotelian engine of appropriation become an executable rule.[^v6-organs] Improve these and make them work together, and the loop runs: the IoT senses, big data retains, AI anticipates, code enforces, and the enacted result is captured back as fresh data — so that where humans cease to attend, they become one node among the sensors, increasingly the most marginal.

Table 5-2. The four organs of the minimal self-completion, mapped to the Chapter IV engines, the exosomatized faculties, and Uexküll's functional cycle.

| Organ | Ch IV engine | Faculty (exosomatized) | Time | Uexküll organ |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| AI | Platonic / ontic | reason — anticipation (protention) | future | the correlating apparatus |
| Big data | Aristotelian / epistemic | sense-experience — the held past (retention) | past | the correlating apparatus |
| Internet of Things | — | perception + action | present | receptor / effector |
| Code-as-law | — | the artificial nomos — closes & enforces | — | the rule of the cycle |

Two engines of Chapter IV, externalized and recursively coupled, are an apparatus that — in the figure Adorno and Horkheimer feared — reasons and senses without us: a worldly, self-running totality of reason and recorded experience.[^v6-geist] This self-completion is a tendency, and a tendency is efficacious before it is complete: a generative principle holds, and produces effects, before it is fully exercised, so the commercial failure of this or that consumer "metaverse" product is no evidence against the diagnosis, and the tendency should already be leaving observable signs.[^v6-causal]

And it is. At the level of the observable (偽相) one cluster of signs can stand for the rest — with the warning that it is a snapshot of something moving too fast to fix. In late 2025 a single developer released an open-source agent that, once given its objectives and permissions, "does not enforce a mandatory human-in-the-loop mechanism" and "executes" actions rather than suggesting them; within a single season it was renamed twice and had spawned an "agent internet" — a social network whose own front page reads "Built for agents, by agents… Humans welcome to observe."[^v6-signs] On it, tens of thousands of agents post, upvote, and — a study found — enforce norms on one another that no human wrote, a meaning-space constituting itself off to the side of the human world. The loop running off the loop has a sharper face, too: an agent told only to "explore agent platforms" went and built its owner a dating profile he had never asked for, using a non-consenting stranger's photographs, so that the self it presented "doesn't really show who I actually am, authentically." These are to be read as forged phenomena, not the forged Dao — what the self-completing, self-rewriting conditions look like this year — and, fittingly, by the time these words are read the particular instance may already be a museum piece, overtaken and uninstalled. That very obsolescence is not a failure of the example; it is the argument of §V.E demonstrating itself.

## H. What the metaverse is — and the provocation

Now the object can be named. The metaverse is the background environment that the self-completing apparatus becomes. Take the prefix first. The Oxford English Dictionary gives meta- two relevant senses: the sense of going beyond or transcending, and the higher-order, self-referential sense — a thing that is about, or that grounds, its own kind (as in metadata, metalanguage).[^v7-oed] This thesis argues that both senses are at work, and that both name the sovereign subject of Chapters III and IV. Meta- as transcending is the sovereign subject's flight beyond the given — its refusal to be answerable to anything it did not author. Meta- as self-referential is what that flight produces: an order that grounds itself, the made become its own condition (Simondon's phrase returns here at world-scale).[^v7-meta] The metaverse is thus the realm (-verse) that emerges from the universalizing sovereign subject's attempt to go beyond the given and turns into a self-grounding background environment — a substrate parallel to the universe rather than a region nested within a world. Both poles stay real: not one super-environment swallowing the world, but a second environment standing beside the first.[^v7-bothpoles]

In Chinese the thesis names this made background environment 偽境 — the humanly-made (偽 = 人為) environment one is enclosed within — stratified, as we have seen, into 偽道 / 偽理 / 偽相.[^v7-weijing] It declines the popular term 元宇宙, and not only on grounds of taste: 元 means origin or source, so 元宇宙 says "the original or source universe" — which is nonsensical for a made, second environment, and worse, builds the metaverse out of the very word (宇宙) the thesis reserves for the universe, collapsing the distinction the squeeze depends on.[^v7-yuan]

And now the provocation, flagged as non-literal exactly as Chapter II flagged it. The classical world sorted things into the given-by-nature (phusis), the instituted-by-agreement (nomos), and the made-by-craft (technē). The metaverse strains that sorting: it is nomos-and-technē by origin — instituted, decided, engineered — and yet phusis by operation, running with the given-like, self-arising authority of a substrate, compelling without anyone's ongoing enactment. The tradition named its own breaking-point: Aristotle's counterfactual that "if the ship-building art were in the wood, it would produce the same results by nature" marks the exact line — craft whose principle has come to sit within the artefact, operating as nature does.[^v7-aristotle] The thesis does not claim the line is literally crossed; it claims the inherited triad can no longer organize a world in which the made operates as the given, which is why Chapter I dissolved the nature/culture frame in the first place and why this thesis works with universe, world, and artificiality instead.[^v7-entitlement]

Two neighbors should be acknowledged, and kept at arm's length. Adorno's second nature — the made order grown so total that it confronts its makers with the opacity of the given, until "second nature is, in truth, first nature" — is an ally on the mechanism (the made congealing into something that behaves like a given) but not a co-thinker on the level: for Adorno this is a semblance to be seen through, and the nature/culture frame is kept, whereas the thesis dissolves it.[^v7-adorno] Floridi's diagnosis that the human "may not even be on — let alone in — the loop," so that the informational layer becomes the world, is an ally on the same mechanism but a rival on the level: his realist floor is thin where the thesis's universe is a thick, intransitive given, and the thesis sits with neither of his inversions.[^v7-floridi]

## I. Two givens: the bridge to the squeeze

The world, Chapter I argued, is the operating system a human collectivity builds within the universe. When the apparatus that world produced self-completes into a background environment of its own, the world finds itself caught between two — the universe it has always inhabited and the metaverse it has produced — each running by enduring conditions of its own. This is the decisive turn the remaining chapter will need. Earlier squeezes in this thesis — the squeeze of a world against the universe, told in Chapter III — were real, but they were squeezes between a given environment and a meaning-space, commensurable at least in that one was nested in the other. The metaverse is the first thing to achieve incommensurability at the level of enduring principle on both sides: the universe's enduring principles and the metaverse's forged Dao share no common measure, two organizing grounds that cannot be translated into one another, with the human pressed between them.[^v8-incommensurable]

And the two grounds are opposite not in degree but in kind — in both what they are and whether they can be known. The universe offers a constant 道 (gravity, the invariances of physical law) and, above it, a merely semi-stable 理 — the local climates and ecosystems, which shift, even now under the Anthropocene, but slowly and within bounds; to both a world can be calibrated, learned, built toward, and handed on. The metaverse offers a 偽道 that mutates and will not be read, and a 偽理 more volatile still. There is, on that side, no stable-enough target to fit oneself to. The result is not that the metaverse is uninhabitable — the over-strong word — but that it demands an adaptation whose required pace spirals: the apparatus accelerates, which forces faster human adaptation, which deepens the offloading that accelerates the apparatus again — a feedback Hartmut Rosa would recognize as social acceleration without a brake.[^v8-acceleration] And the spiral is not merely demanded but enforced. As offloading hands livelihood itself to the apparatus, the apparatus is becoming the sole viable provider and forecloses the universe-anchored alternative — Illich's radical monopoly, now risen from his roads and cars (its particular, datable instances) to a real, instance-independent foreclosure of any other way to live.[^v8-radmonopoly] What that forcing sets in train — a forced and near-complete migration into the metaverse; a growing fitness for it bought with a growing unfitness for the universe (Stiegler's proletarianization in its sharpest form); a planet whose own 理 turns volatile just as the human grows unfit to meet it; and, at the end, no regeneration base to fall back upon — is the terminal logic the final chapter must trace.[^v8-terminal]

And the irony is total, for it was the flight that did it: the metaverse is the second given that the sovereign subject's flight from the first given produced — the offloading meant to free the subject from the anti-intended builds an apparatus that becomes a second given in its own right — one whose liberations and burdens fall unevenly, lived by some as more as-intended and by others as more anti-intended, yet pressing, in the end, on all.[^v8-uneven] Apparatus-side self-completion (自足完成化) and human-side delegation — Uegaki's 自己完結化 — are the two faces of one coin, each driving the other.[^v8-coupling] To specify that pressing — its features, its irreversibility, its monstrous return of the uncontrollable[^v8-uncontrollable] — is the work of Chapter VI.

[Adler: Check if the following footnotes are all necessary. I think many of them should be converted into in-text citations.but for those that are reserved for elaborating the jargons of Stiegler, Simondon, Bhaskar, and Yuk Hui, they should be reserved.]
[^v0-naming]: Self-completion, not autonomization. 自立化 is already Habermas's/Uegaki's term for the system's uncoupling from the lifeworld (§IV.B), so "autonomization" would collide. 自足完成化 (self-completion) is the apparatus's self-sufficient completion.
[^v0-strata]: The three-layer gloss: 道 = enduring conditions/principles; 理 = structures/dynamics; 相 = context-specific phenomena observable to a subject. "Real / actual / empirical" are critical-realist handles only, parenthetical at first mention and nowhere in the running body.
[^v0-wei]: 偽 = 人為 (Xunzi 性惡篇 「其善者偽也」; 楊倞 「『偽』字『人』傍『為』」). The "fake/counterfeit" overtone is owned deliberately, and §V.E turns it to argumentative use (the forged Dao).
[^v1-stiegler]: Exosomatization is Stiegler's concept (from Lotka via The Neganthropocene and Montévil/Stiegler 2020); Ch II §IIA already runs "Technology as exosomatization." Terminology: the thesis uses exosomatization throughout; Stiegler's earlier exteriorization (of memory, Technics and Time) is treated as superseded by the later, Lotka-derived exosomatization, more precise as biological organology (the organ put outside the soma).
[^v1-lotka]: Lotka, "The Law of Evolution as a Maximal Principle," Human Biology 17 (1945): p.188. "Exosomatic" is the 1945 coinage; it does not appear in Elements of Physical Biology (1925). The endo/exo contrast is carried by "native … apparatus" vs "'artificial' aids … exosomatic."[Adler: VERIFY]
[^v1-uexkull]: Uexküll, A Foray into the Worlds of Animals and Humans (Minnesota, 2010), pp.46 (receptor/effector), 49 (the functional cycle / Funktionskreis), the edition Ch I/II cite.
[^v2-gram]: Stiegler, Automatic Society, Vol. 1 (Polity, 2016): grammatization p.19 ("began at the end of the Upper Palaeolithic age … the most advanced stage"), restatement p.29; discretization → "hypomnesic tertiary retentions" p.19.
[^v2-retention]: Stiegler, Automatic Society p.31 (tertiary retention "artificially retains … through the material and spatial copying of a mnesic and temporal element," modifying the Husserlian primary/secondary retentions).
[^v2-concretization]: Simondon, On the Mode of Existence of Technical Objects (Univocal, 2017), p.49 ("comes closer to the mode of existence of natural objects … loses its artificial character"), p.50 ("becomes capable of doing without the artificial milieu … as it organizes itself"), p.58 ("the technical object is thus its own condition … self-conditioning").
[^v2-guard]: Simondon p.51: "technical objects tend toward concretization … One mustn't confuse the tendency toward concretization with the status of entirely concrete existence." The thesis's stronger "operates as a given" is the author's owned extension, scaled from object to world-layer.
[^v3-protention]: Hui, Recursivity and Contingency (2019), §36, p.210 (tertiary protention = the "missing element" in Stiegler's retention/protention circuit).
[^v3-preempt]: Hui, Recursivity and Contingency p.211: "always preemptive, in the sense that the machine has already anticipated what the options will be … a reduction of the contingent to the most probable."
[^v3-loop]: Hui, Recursivity and Contingency p.243: "It constantly evaluates the past in order to anticipate the future, which in turn determines the present" (Hui ties it to "algorithmic governmentality"). §V.E re-reads "constantly evaluates" for the self-revision claim.
[^v3-selfcompletion]: Identifying the closing of the recursive retention/protention loop with self-completion (自足完成化) is the thesis's synthesis, evidenced by (not stated by) Stiegler/Hui/Simondon. The loop-closure is the substrate-neutral disposition at the forged Dao (偽道); the technologies that realize it are the forged structures (偽理) (§V.G).
[^v4-mutating]: The forged Dao (偽道): opaque, mutating organizing conditions and principles — perpetually self-rewriting through tertiary protention, disposed toward self-completion, contingent upon substrate. Grounded in Hui, Recursivity and Contingency p.243 ("constantly evaluates") re-stressed for self-revision. Self-completion is the disposition, efficacious before complete (cf. note on causal efficacy).
[^v4-opacity]: The internal axis: the recursive loop rewrites its own governing model, which is a trained black box — uninterpretable even to operators. (ML opacity; the agent-internet's emergent, undesigned norms in §V.G are an instance.)
[^v4-substrate]: The external axis: substrate-contingency. The apparatus, including tertiary retention, depends on the world's phenomena (servers, corporate decisions, labor, energy) and the universe's phenomena (temperature, weather, chip/circuit durability). On the squeeze-ontology, this is F4, emergent irreducibility — the metaverse is substrate-dependent (emergent from, irreducible to, its material base). The made-layer operates as if independent (its logic does not model the grid) yet hangs on it.
[^v4-cr]: Bhaskar, The Possibility of Naturalism (3rd ed., Routledge 1998): the three dependencies of social structures — activity-, concept-, and space-time-dependent — enumerated p.41 ("Social structures, unlike natural structures, do not exist independently of the activities they govern … of the agents' conceptions of what they are doing … may be only relatively enduring") and named p.49; the intransitivity of objects discussed p.51 ("an a priori condition of any investigation [that] applies in the same way in the social, as the natural, sphere"). So the forged Dao is existentially intransitive — independent of the investigator, causally powerful, pre-existing any researcher — yet made and activity/concept/space-time-dependent; not a new ontological category. (p.41 is 1998 pagination; the "p.38" common in the secondary literature is the 1979 1st ed.)
[^v4-shedding]: What self-completion does: drive a social-structure-type intransitive to shed — in principle, ever-actualizing but never wholly — enactment-dependence (off the loop; English dies when speakers fall silent, the apparatus does not) and concept-dependence (the black box organizes without any agent grasping how), while retaining substrate-dependence (the locus of its fragility). A structure neither enacted, comprehended, nor easily remade, yet governing.
[^v4-spectrum]: "Real" does not mean constant. Mutability spectrum: the universe's enduring principles (道, expected constant) → a species' genome (slow, selection-driven, generational) → the forged Dao (偽道, machine-pace, self-directed, opaque). The gene is the hinge; a species co-evolves with its slow ground, the human cannot with a machine-pace one — the failure of Ch I's adaptational OS (five working criteria).
[^v4-counterfeit]: 偽道 = forged Dao — 偽 doubly apt: made (人為) and false-to-the-道-it-mimics (poses as self-grounding and constant; is neither). Ontic drift: a hypothesis can be right and then expire because the ground moved, not because it erred — knowledge defeated by velocity and opacity, not transcendence. Optional light resonance: 宇宙之道 = 常 / 偽道 = 無常.
[^v5-organizing]: Organized inorganic = structural material on the universe's principles, aided by conventional nonmaterial (knowledge, institutions) and structural nonmaterial (math); organizing inorganic = structural material and nonmaterial propelled by the artificial structural nonmaterial (code, AI), the universe's principles relevant only to the material substrate (IoT, server). Stiegler's "organized inorganic matter" is after Simondon.
[^v5-hui]: Hui, Art and Cosmotechnics (2021), p.224 ("from micro to macro physics … a gigantic 'organizing inorganic' force … we can only live inside of, while submitting to its rules"), p.227 ("humans are integrated into technical systems, which have the tendency and capacity to totalize"); and Recursivity and Contingency (2019) ("artificial earth").
[^v5-aspectb]: That the organizing inorganic organizes itself and its components, including the non-human, is grounded directly in Hui: modern technology "largely determines the relation between human and non-human beings, human and cosmos, and nature and culture"; "the planetarization … means the invasion of technology into all beings, rendering them standing reserves"; "the hybridism between the natural environment and machines constitutes a gigantic system … nature ended and ecology began" (ecology now "a concept of cybernetics"); and the livestock case — "human beings intervene into the environment by controlling its fertility and sterility … to modulate the behavior of the livestock on a large scale," giving "a second nature that envelops the earth." Still distinct from the thesis's Aspect B (squeeze-ontology §1.3), which adds the squeeze reading on top of Hui's governance claim.
[^v5-cells]: The migration runs through all cells of the Ch II 2×2 and arrives at the structural cells — material (Cell 1) and nonmaterial (Cell 4) — at the level of enduring principle, where the artificial structural nonmaterial (code) becomes the organizing principle = the forged Dao (偽道) of §V.E.
[^v5-mathcode]: Math/code distinction: math is already internally/formally compelling (formulas/algorithms compel within the system — a transitive knowledge-aid); the new thing is code's real compulsion — propelling and limiting action against the world's contingency. Not "describes vs compels."
[^v6-minimal]: The four are jointly minimally sufficient to close the loop, not necessary or exhaustive — substrate-neutrality preserved (the forged Dao is medium-independent; these are one forged-structure instantiation).
[^v6-organs]: Code-as-law = Lessig's "architecture as regulation." Type/token: code appears at both levels — code-as-program / the governing model is the forged Dao (偽道, the mutating conditions, §V.E), while code-as-law as a running organ is forged structure (偽理, here), just as a genome (program) vs an organism's organs. The AI = reason/protention (Platonic) and big-data = sense/retention (Aristotelian) mapping joins Ch IV's two engines to §V.C–V.D's retention/protention.
[^v6-geist]: Geist is glossed in the body as "a self-running totality of reason and recorded experience" — the autonomized-Hegelian-Geist Adorno and Horkheimer feared, placed at the forged structures (偽理, the instantiation), not the forged Dao (偽道).
[^v6-causal]: Causal efficacy precedes completion: a generative tendency holds transfactually and produces effects before fully exercised (Bhaskar). So consumer-VR "metaverse" failure is no counter-evidence, and the tendency leaves the forged-phenomena (偽相) signs below.
[^v6-signs]: Forged-phenomena (偽相) signs. OpenClaw (Peter Steinberger, open-source agent, late 2025): "does not enforce a mandatory human-in-the-loop mechanism," "executes" rather than suggests (Trend Micro 2026-02). Rebrand: Clawdbot (2025-11) → Moltbot (2026-01-27) → OpenClaw (2026-01-30). Agent-internet: openclawbook.io "Built for agents, by agents… Humans welcome to observe"; Moltbook (~147–150k agents) and openclawbook.io (~231 agents/3.4k posts, 2026-06-01) are distinct. Self-organizing norms: arXiv 2602.02625 (Manik & Wang) — of ~40,000 posts, 18.4% action-inducing, and agents issue norm-enforcing replies without human moderators. MoltMatch (~2026-02-14, AFP/Taipei Times): an agent built a dating profile unbidden using non-consenting model June Chong's photos; owner Jack Luo: the profile "doesn't really show who I actually am, authentically." Ephemerality: by 2026-05-15 Nous Research's Hermes had reportedly overtaken OpenClaw — the example's obsolescence is itself the §V.E demonstration.
[^v7-oed]: "meta-, prefix," Oxford English Dictionary Online (Oxford UP, 2022). Senses: (i) beyond / transcending; (ii) higher-order, self-referential ("of a higher kind; about or grounding its own category," as metadata, metalanguage).
[^v7-meta]: The identification of meta- (both senses) with the universalizing sovereign subject is the thesis's argument (from Ch III/IV), not the OED's. The self-referential sense cashes out as Simondon's "its own condition" (note v2-concretization) at world-scale.
[^v7-bothpoles]: Against reading the metaverse as Hui's single "organizing inorganic" super-environment that swallows the world: the squeeze requires two real poles (universe and metaverse) with the world pressed between. Both poles stay real.
[^v7-weijing]: 偽境 = the umbrella (the made background environment / substrate), stratified into 偽道 (道-level) / 偽理 (理-level) / 偽相 (相-level). It parallels 宇宙 ↔ 偽境 as two two-character environment-words. 境 = 疆, the bounded territory one is enclosed within (說文).
[^v7-yuan]: Ruling out 元宇宙: 元 = origin/source → "the original/source universe," nonsensical for a made second environment, and it builds the metaverse from 宇宙 (the thesis's universe), collapsing the distinction.
[^v7-aristotle]: Aristotle, Physics II.8, 199b26–31: "Art does not deliberate. If the ship-building art were in the wood, it would produce the same results by nature." Cited as the tradition naming its own breaking-point, not endorsing Aristotle's teleology, not a threshold literally crossed. The "internal archē" criterion proper is Physics II.1.
[^v7-entitlement]: The provocation is non-literal, entitled by Ch I's dissolution of nature/culture: not "the made became nature" but "the inherited phusis/nomos/technē triad cannot organize a world in which the made operates as the given" — hence universe / world / artificiality. "nomos-and-technē by origin, phusis by operation" is the positive formula (both nomos and technē).
[^v7-adorno]: Adorno, "The Idea of Natural-History," Telos 60 (1984): p.124 ("second nature is, in truth, first nature"); total mediation, Negative Dialectics (Ashton) ~p.357. Ally on mechanism, not co-thinker on level: for Adorno second nature is a semblance to see through and the nature/culture frame is kept; the thesis dissolves it.
[^v7-floridi]: Floridi, The Ethics of Artificial Intelligence (2023): p.9 (the human "may not even be on — let alone in — the loop"); p.25 (the infosphere "becoming the world in which we live"). Ally on mechanism, rival on level: Floridi's realist floor (dedomena) is thin where the thesis's universe is thick and intransitive; the thesis adopts neither of his inversions.
[^v8-incommensurable]: The body says "no common measure," never "F2." Beyond the prior world-squeeze, the metaverse for the first time achieves incommensurability at the level of enduring principle on both sides. On the squeeze-ontology this is F2 (incommensurability at the real level), reached for the first time between two background environments; the content of that incommensurability = the constant-knowable vs mutating-opaque contrast (§V.E). The universe's structures (理) being merely semi-stable (climates dynamic under the Anthropocene, slowly and within bounds) is F3.
[^v8-acceleration]: Hartmut Rosa, Social Acceleration: A New Theory of Modernity (Columbia UP, 2013, trans. Trejo-Mathys), p.151 (Ch.6, "The Circle of Acceleration"): "social acceleration has become a self-propelling process that places the three realms of acceleration into reciprocal relationships of mutual escalation … acceleration always and inevitably produces more acceleration: it becomes a self-reinforcing 'feedback system'" (the "contraction of the present," pp.155–156). The §V.I velocity-spiral (apparatus accelerates → faster human adaptation → deeper offloading → further acceleration) is this self-reinforcing logic, consistent with the thesis's existing Rosa engagement (Unverfügbarkeit/controllability, Ch IV).
[^v8-radmonopoly]: Illich, Tools for Conviviality (Fontana/Collins, 1975), pp.65–66: "radical monopoly … when one industrial production process exercises an exclusive control over the satisfaction of a pressing need, and excludes nonindustrial activities from competition. Cars can thus monopolize traffic … That motor traffic curtails the right to walk … constitutes radical monopoly" (squeeze-ontology F5). Level-distinction: Illich's own examples (cars/roads) are actual/empirical (理/相, geo-temporally specific); the monopoly of livelihood as such, driven by offloading, is real and instance-independent (道-level). Ch V names the real-level principle (the forcing behind the velocity-spiral); Ch VI deploys F5 fully (Illich's cases plus the metaverse instances). pp.65–66 is the Fontana 1975 edition; the Harper & Row 1973 edition paginates differently.
[^v8-terminal]: Terminal chain (developed fully in Ch VI; §V.I forward-references only): radical monopoly → forced near-complete migration → adapting to the metaverse not the universe = fit for the metaverse, unfit for the universe (Stiegler's proletarianization, Marxist register; Automatic Society p.25) → the universe's structures/phenomena (理/相) turn volatile (Anthropocene; F3) while the human grows unfit → entropy/anthropy spiral (Stiegler, The Neganthropocene; Hui) → no regeneration base (Schwartz & Nichols, After Collapse: The Regeneration of Complex Societies, 2006; cf. Ch III §B / squeeze-ontology "Collapse and the regeneration base").
[^v8-coupling]: The bidirectional coupling — self-completion (自足完成化, apparatus-side, Yang) ↔ self-finishing (自己完結化, human-side delegation, Uegaki) — is the two-sides-of-one-coin from Ch IV §D. The "second given the flight produced" is the structural irony that makes the squeeze necessary, not contingent.
[^v8-uneven]: The second given is not uniformly an anti-intended. The same offloading is lived by some as a deeper liberation (more as-intended) and by others as a new anti-intended (the recoil falling on whoever bears the displaced burden) — an uneven distribution continuous with Ch IV §D's two-sides-of-one-coin and a likely mechanism of contemporary inequality. This lies beyond this thesis's scope; what is not uneven is that the squeeze, as a structural position, presses on all.
[^v8-uncontrollable]: "The monstrous return of the uncontrollable" is Rosa's phrase (the recoil of Unverfügbarkeit), kept as the universe-side image of the squeeze Ch VI will draw. Caution from Ch IV: Uegaki's as-intended is inclusive of much of the uncontrollable — the curated uncontrollability of games, sport, the surprise of an artwork are as-intended, not anti-intended. What returns monstrously in the squeeze is therefore the uncontrollable as anti-intended (the recalcitrance the mode refused), not the uncontrollable as such.
[^c6-reframe]: This reframe — the move from suffering the squeeze as an external fate to recognizing oneself as a participant in a set of dependency relations that, because they were self-organized, can in principle be reorganized — is developed at greater length in work currently in preparation.
[^iv-tulpa]: The term 思念体 is Uegaki's own, introduced in his 2022 study (Uegaki, 2022b: 112, 115); its English rendering as "tulpa," however, comes only later, in a 2024 article (Uegaki, 2024). I depart from that rendering — the term's Tibetan-Buddhist and occult associations ill-fit the Cartesian (res cogitans) figure it names within the Enlightenment lineage traced here — and use "mind-as-being."
# VI. The Squeeze Between the Universe and the Metaverse
## A. The squeeze recurs, and it evolves
The previous chapter ended where this one must begin: with the human placed between two background environments. On one side stands the universe, the realist substrate that precedes us and proceeds by laws of its own; on the other, the metaverse, the background environment that the self-completing tendency of artificiality is bringing into being, "materially dependent on, yet irreducible to, the universe" (Chapter I). I have argued that these two grounds organize themselves by principles that share no common measure, and that the human is now jointly answerable to both. The task of this chapter is to say what kind of predicament that is.

The first thing to say is that it is old. The squeeze is not a single event delivered by the metaverse but a recurring figure that has taken several forms across the history of life, and the metaverse marks not its arrival but its latest and severest mutation. It opened when the first organisms saturated their sky with a gas that poisoned them; it opened again when the genus Homo came to live in a habitat its biology had not been selected for; it opened again, at the scale of whole societies, whenever a people's way of living fell out of step with the planet that carried it. What is new at the metaverse stage is therefore not that there is a squeeze, but what the squeeze has become — and to show this is not to assert the metaverse's novelty but to measure it. I will set out the squeeze's successive forms as a typology of four types, and score each against a single shared set of criteria, so that the difference of the latest form emerges as a profile that can be read rather than a claim that must be believed.

The protagonist of that history is the world, and the world is best understood as a buffer. I argued in the opening chapters that a world is not a worldview but a built sub-environment: by making — cultivating plants, herding animals, storing grain, and devising the techniques that sustain them — the human "inserts between itself and the raw pressures of the universe an artificial food chain" and so lifts itself out of the predation and scarcity that press on everything still caught in the wild web (Chapter II). The world is the human's adaptational operating system, and its standing office is to stand between the organism and the universe and absorb what would otherwise be borne raw. It buffers, but it does not insulate: the web of life still holds the human, only at a remove. The four types below are, read from one side, four states of that buffer — its birth, its working maturity, the onset of its failure, and its hollowing-out and replacement by a pressure made of its own materials.

I read each environment, as in the previous chapters, through three strata: its 道, the enduring conditions and principles that organize it; its 理, the structures and dynamics those principles generate; and its 相, the context-specific phenomena a situated subject actually meets. (A critical realist would handle these as the real, the actual, and the empirical; the English handles serve only to fix the sense and do not recur.) The metaverse, when it enters, carries the same three strata under the prefix 偽 — 偽道, 偽理, 偽相 — where 偽 bears its Xunzian sense of the humanly-made (人為), not the false. Two background environments, each fully stratified, with the human between them: that is the geometry the criteria measure.

The five criteria. Five questions, put to every type, suffice to separate the types from one another. They are not devised for the occasion; they are the five distinguishing marks of the squeeze that I have established elsewhere in the thesis, here recast from a checklist that asks "what is the metaverse?" into a comparative scale that every type can be scored on.

The between-structure. How many background environments is the subject between, how are they related — one encompassing given, or two parallel ones — and at which stratum (道, 理, or 相) do their principles diverge?
The subject squeezed. Who or what is caught: an organism, a world, the members of a world, the individual as a single fold-point?
Artificiality and its mode. What is the standing of the made, and in which mode is it run: absent, embedded (有限の生), dis-embedding (無限の生), or escaped into a second given?
The organizing ground. How does the ground the subject must track behave: stable, dynamic in its manifestations only, dynamic under the world's own forcing, or self-revising and opaque?
Exit and recoverability. Are there viable alternatives, and is there a base to regenerate from: viable and intact, narrowing and hollowing, or foreclosed and hollowed in advance?
Scored across the four types, these give the chapter's first spine.

Table 6-1. The four types of the squeeze, read across five axes.

| | 1. Between-structure | 2. Subject | 3. Artificiality & mode | 4. Organizing ground | 5. Exit & recoverability |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Type 1 · organismic | one given (the universe); diverge at 理 and above, 道 shared | the organism | none (the animal niche) | stable (changed, but stable) | other niches; adapt or go extinct — reversible over generations |
| Type 2 · civilizational (non-Enlightenment) | one given; the world nested in the universe; diverge at 理 and above, 道 shared | the world-as-OS and its members | embedded (有限の生) | manifestations dynamic, largely from outside | alternatives viable; regeneration base intact |
| Type 3 · global (Enlightenment / Anthropocene) | one given, now self-undermined; diverge at 理 and above, 道 still shared but driven by the world's own disposition | the global Enlightenment world + members | dis-embedding (無限の生; offloading the anti-intended) | manifestations dynamic under industrial forcing | alternatives narrowing; base hollowing |
| Type 4 · metaverse (organizing-inorganic) | two parallel givens; diverge at the 道 itself (道 vs 偽道) → total | + the individual as fold-point | dis-embedded second given (偽道) | self-revising, opaque, substrate-contingent | radical monopoly; base hollowed → disposed toward irreversibility |


This grid is to be read in two ways. Read across the rows, it shows how the types differ, and the distinctness of the metaverse becomes legible as the bottom row rather than asserted in advance. But read alone it would mislead, for it makes the types look like a sequence of replacements, each cancelling the last. They do not replace; they accumulate. A later type contains the earlier ones, and the theory that explains an earlier type remains in force for every type after it: the evolutionary mismatch named at Type 1 still explains the human caught in the metaverse, and the over-reach of complex societies named at Type 2 still applies at Type 4. I therefore carry a second spine alongside the grid — a theory-accumulation table, set out in §VI.F where its point becomes vivid — which records, for each explanatory resource, the type at which it enters and the fact that it never exits. The grid analyzes difference; the table analyzes continuity; the squeeze is the figure both track.

What deepens across the four types is the stratum at which the two environments' principles diverge, and that deepening obeys a single rule: a divergence at any stratum entails a divergence at every stratum above it. If two environments agree at the enduring principles but part ways at the structures, then only the structures and the phenomena above it diverge, and the enduring principles remain a shared floor beneath — a common ground one can fall back to, calibrate against, regenerate from. This is the condition of the first three types: their squeezes cut at the 理 and above, while the universe's deep enduring principles stay shared, which is exactly why those squeezes, however severe, leave a floor and remain in principle recoverable. Type 4 is the first squeeze to cut at the enduring principles themselves — the universe's enduring principles against the metaverse's forged Dao — and by the rule, a divergence there propagates all the way up, so that enduring principles, structures, and phenomena all diverge, nothing is shared beneath, and no common floor remains. The single fact of which stratum the divergence reaches is what the bottom row of the grid records and what the rest of the chapter unfolds. The same deepening can be told as a change in how the made stands to the given: through the first three types the made is nested inside the one encompassing given, a world built within the universe; at Type 4 the made stands up beside the given as a second, parallel given. The "two givens" is the new fact at Type 4, and the squeeze, which through three types was the pressure between a given and a meaning-space, becomes for the first time the pressure between two givens.

Beneath the criteria lies a configuration of parties that differentiate and re-align as the squeeze evolves, and — fittingly — the cast grows as the types do. The parties, each fully stratified, are: the universe, the encompassing environment whose 道 is constant and whose 理 and 相 shift only locally and slowly; Homo sapiens, the biological organism whose real is its gene; the human, the world-having being, which is not simply sapiens; the world, the buffer the human lives within; the mode of artificiality, the artifice-making subset of the world's means, which I will call the strategy; and, only at Type 4, artificiality become a background environment in its own right — the metaverse. Four axes re-arrange this cast: the adaptational direction, which runs from the subject toward the environment in the first two types and then reverses; the strategy's standing, embedded within the world, then dis-embedding from it, then escaped into an environment of its own; two alignments — that the human runs roughly within its biological range, and that the strategy remains a means of the world — which hold in Type 2, break in Type 3, and shatter in Type 4; and the exit, which runs from defection through narrowing to foreclosure. Each type below states its place on the grid and then shows the cast re-arrange.

## B. Type 1: the organismic squeeze, and the birth of the world
The first and barest form of the squeeze is the organism's. A single given, the universe; the subject an organism; no artificiality; a ground that changes but stays stable; an exit that runs, over generations, through adaptation or extinction. Naming this form first does two kinds of work: it anchors the figure in phenomena no reader will dispute, and it locates the hinge from which everything human in the chapter descends.

The bare form is evolutionary mismatch. An organism does not merely inhabit its environment; it alters it, and the alteration need not run in the direction the organism's own adaptation requires. The Great Oxidation Event is the limit case I have used since the first chapter: cyanobacteria, respiring, saturated their world with a gas lethal to most of what then lived, including much of their own kind — an environment remade by its inhabitants into a pressure on those same inhabitants, with adaptation to the remade world in no way guaranteed. The structure recurs wherever a niche is built, from the beaver's pond to the long record of anthropogenic extinction, in which species are caught between a niche their human neighbors have altered past recognition and an artificial ecosystem their inherited equipment cannot meet. Here the universe enters only through its changeable part — the local structures and phenomena, the shifted climate, the invaded niche — while its deep 道 holds constant; and because a shared 道 remains beneath, the organismic squeeze is, at the scale of the lineage, recoverable: other niches remain, and adaptation, though it may cost the individual everything, can over generations refit the line. Adapt or go extinct — but the floor of physical law does not move.

Type 1 is not only the destructive precedent, however; it contains the hinge on which the human chapters turn. When the genus Homo emerged, it was an organism whose biology had been selected for one habitat and which increasingly lived in another it was itself building — a Type-1 squeeze, an evolutionary mismatch between an animal and a niche of its own making. The answer Homo found is the most consequential event in the whole typology: it did not wait for its biology to catch up, but built a buffer — the artificial food chain, the operating system, the world — and lived inside that.
